You can search across multiple fields in your relational\\n36: database, combine the searches with other lookups, use different language\\n37: configurations and weightings, and rank the results by relevance.\\n38: \\n39: It also now includes trigram support, using the :lookup:`trigram_similar`\\n40: lookup, and the :class:`~django.contrib.postgres.search.TrigramSimilarity` and\\n41: :class:`~django.contrib.postgres.search.TrigramDistance` expressions.\\n42: \\n43: New-style middleware\\n44: --------------------\\n45: \\n46: :doc:`A new style of middleware is introduced </topics/http/middleware>` to\\n47: solve the lack of strict request/response layering of the old-style of\\n48: middleware described in `DEP 0005\\n49: <https://github.com/django/deps/blob/main/final/0005-improved-middleware.rst>`_.\\n50: You'll need to :ref:`adapt old, custom middleware <upgrading-middleware>` and\\n51: switch from the ``MIDDLEWARE_CLASSES`` setting to the new :setting:`MIDDLEWARE`\\n52: setting to take advantage of the improvements.\\n53: \\n54: Official support for Unicode usernames\\n55: --------------------------------------\\n56: \\n57: The :class:`~django.contrib.auth.models.User` model in ``django.contrib.auth``\\n58: originally only accepted ASCII letters and numbers in usernames. Although it\\n59: wasn't a deliberate choice, Unicode characters have always been accepted when\\n60: using Python 3.\\n61: \\n62: The username validator now explicitly accepts Unicode characters by\\n63: default on Python 3 only.\\n64: \\n65: Custom user models may use the new\\n66: :class:`~django.contrib.auth.validators.ASCIIUsernameValidator` or\\n67: :class:`~django.contrib.auth.validators.UnicodeUsernameValidator`.\\n68: \\n69: Minor features\\n70: --------------\\n71: \\n72: :mod:`django.contrib.admin`\\n73: ~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~\\n74: \\n75: * For sites running on a subpath, the default :attr:`URL for the \\\"View site\\\"\\n76:   link <django.contrib.admin.AdminSite.site_url>` at the top of each admin page\\n77:   will now point to ``request.META['SCRIPT_NAME']`` if set, instead of ``/``.\\n78: \\n79: * The success message that appears after adding or editing an object now\\n80:   contains a link to the object's change form.\\n81: \\n82: * All inline JavaScript is removed so you can enable the\\n83:   ``Content-Security-Policy`` HTTP header if you wish.\\n84: \\n85: * The new :attr:`InlineModelAdmin.classes\\n86:   <django.contrib.admin.InlineModelAdmin.classes>` attribute allows specifying\\n87:   classes on inline fieldsets. Inlines with a ``collapse`` class will be\\n88:   initially collapsed and their header will have a small \\\"show\\\" link.\\n89: \\n90: * If a user doesn't have the add permission, the ``object-tools`` block on a\\n91:   model's changelist will now be rendered (without the add button). This makes\\n92:   it easier to add custom tools in this case.\\n93: \\n94: * The :class:`~django.contrib.admin.models.LogEntry` model now stores change\\n95:   messages in a JSON structure so that the message can be dynamically\\n96:   translated using the current active language. A new\\n97:   ``LogEntry.get_change_message()`` method is now the preferred way of\\n98:   retrieving the change message.\\n99: \\n100: * Selected objects for fields in ``ModelAdmin.raw_id_fields`` now have a link\\n101:   to object's change form.\\n102: \\n103: * Added \\\"No date\\\" and \\\"Has date\\\" choices for ``DateFieldListFilter`` if the\\n104:   field is nullable.\\n105: \\n106: * The jQuery library embedded in the admin is upgraded from version 2.1.4 to\\n107:   2.2.3.\\n108: \\n109: :mod:`django.contrib.auth`\\n110: ~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~\\n111: \\n112: * Added support for the :ref:`Argon2 password hash <argon2_usage>`. It's\\n113:   recommended over PBKDF2, however, it's not the default as it requires a\\n114:   third-party library.\\n115: \\n116: * The default iteration count for the PBKDF2 password hasher has been increased\\n117:   by 25%. This backwards compatible change will not affect users who have\\n118:   subclassed ``django.contrib.auth.hashers.PBKDF2PasswordHasher`` to change the\\n119:   default value.\\n120: \\n121: * The ``django.contrib.auth.views.logout()`` view sends \\\"no-cache\\\" headers\\n122:   to prevent an issue where Safari caches redirects and prevents a user from\\n123:   being able to log out.\\n124: \\n125: * Added the optional ``backend`` argument to :func:`django.contrib.auth.login`\\n126:   to allow using it without credentials.\\n127: \\n128: * The new :setting:`LOGOUT_REDIRECT_URL` setting controls the redirect of the\\n129:   ``django.contrib.auth.views.logout()`` view, if the view doesn't get a\\n130:   ``next_page`` argument.\\n131: \\n132: * The new ``redirect_authenticated_user`` parameter for the\\n133:   ``django.contrib.auth.views.login()`` view allows redirecting\\n134:   authenticated users visiting the login page.\\n135: \\n136: * The new :class:`~django.contrib.auth.backends.AllowAllUsersModelBackend` and\\n137:   :class:`~django.contrib.auth.backends.AllowAllUsersRemoteUserBackend` ignore\\n138:   the value of ``User.is_active``, We've\n12: :ref:`dropped some features <removed-features-1.10>` that have reached the end\n13: of their deprecation cycle, and we've :ref:`begun the deprecation process for\n14: some features <deprecated-features-1.10>`.\n15: \n16: See the :doc:`/howto/upgrade-version` guide if you're updating an existing\n17: project.\n18: \n19: Python compatibility\n20: ====================\n21: \n22: Like Django 1.9, Django 1.10 requires Python 2.7, 3.4, or 3.5. You can search across multiple fields in your relational\n36: database, combine the searches with other lookups, use different language\n37: configurations and weightings, and rank the results by relevance.\n38: \n39: It also now includes trigram support, using the :lookup:`trigram_similar`\n40: lookup, and the :class:`~django.contrib.postgres.search.TrigramSimilarity` and\n41: :class:`~django.contrib.postgres.search.TrigramDistance` expressions.\n42: \n43: New-style middleware\n44: --------------------\n45: \n46: :doc:`A new style of middleware is introduced </topics/http/middleware>` to\n47: solve the lack of strict request/response layering of the old-style of\n48: middleware described in `DEP 0005\n49: <https://github.com/django/deps/blob/main/final/0005-improved-middleware.rst>`_.\n50: You'll need to :ref:`adapt old, custom middleware <upgrading-middleware>` and\n51: switch from the ``MIDDLEWARE_CLASSES`` setting to the new :setting:`MIDDLEWARE`\n52: setting to take advantage of the improvements.\n53: \n54: Official support for Unicode usernames\n55: --------------------------------------\n56: \n57: The :class:`~django.contrib.auth.models.User` model in ``django.contrib.auth``\n58: originally only accepted ASCII letters and numbers in usernames. Although it\n59: wasn't a deliberate choice, Unicode characters have always been accepted when\n60: using Python 3.\n61: \n62: The username validator now explicitly accepts Unicode characters by\n63: default on Python 3 only.\n64: \n65: Custom user models may use the new\n66: :class:`~django.contrib.auth.validators.ASCIIUsernameValidator` or\n67: :class:`~django.contrib.auth.validators.UnicodeUsernameValidator`.\n68: \n69: Minor features\n70: --------------\n71: \n72: :mod:`django.contrib.admin`\n73: ~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~\n74: \n75: * For sites running on a subpath, the default :attr:`URL for the \"View site\"\n76:   link <django.contrib.admin.AdminSite.site_url>` at the top of each admin page\n77:   will now point to ``request.META['SCRIPT_NAME']`` if set, instead of ``/``.\n78: \n79: * The success message that appears after adding or editing an object now\n80:   contains a link to the object's change form.\n81: \n82: * All inline JavaScript is removed so you can enable the\n83:   ``Content-Security-Policy`` HTTP header if you wish.\n84: \n85: * The new :attr:`InlineModelAdmin.classes\n86:   <django.contrib.admin.InlineModelAdmin.classes>` attribute allows specifying\n87:   classes on inline fieldsets. Inlines with a ``collapse`` class will be\n88:   initially collapsed and their header will have a small \"show\" link.\n89: \n90: * If a user doesn't have the add permission, the ``object-tools`` block on a\n91:   model's changelist will now be rendered (without the add button). This makes\n92:   it easier to add custom tools in this case.\n93: \n94: * The :class:`~django.contrib.admin.models.LogEntry` model now stores change\n95:   messages in a JSON structure so that the message can be dynamically\n96:   translated using the current active language. A new\n97:   ``LogEntry.get_change_message()`` method is now the preferred way of\n98:   retrieving the change message.\n99: \n100: * Selected objects for fields in ``ModelAdmin.raw_id_fields`` now have a link\n101:   to object's change form.\n102: \n103: * Added \"No date\" and \"Has date\" choices for ``DateFieldListFilter`` if the\n104:   field is nullable.\n105: \n106: * The jQuery library embedded in the admin is upgraded from version 2.1.4 to\n107:   2.2.3.\n108: \n109: :mod:`django.contrib.auth`\n110: ~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~\n111: \n112: * Added support for the :ref:`Argon2 password hash <argon2_usage>`. It's\n113:   recommended over PBKDF2, however, it's not the default as it requires a\n114:   third-party library.\n115: \n116: * The default iteration count for the PBKDF2 password hasher has been increased\n117:   by 25%. This backwards compatible change will not affect users who have\n118:   subclassed ``django.contrib.auth.hashers.PBKDF2PasswordHasher`` to change the\n119:   default value.\n120: \n121: * The ``django.contrib.auth.views.logout()`` view sends \"no-cache\" headers\n122:   to prevent an issue where Safari caches redirects and prevents a user from\n123:   being able to log out.\n124: \n125: * Added the optional ``backend`` argument to :func:`django.contrib.auth.login`\n126:   to allow using it without credentials.\n127: \n128: * The new :setting:`LOGOUT_REDIRECT_URL` setting controls the redirect of the\n129:   ``django.contrib.auth.views.logout()`` view, if the view doesn't get a\n130:   ``next_page`` argument.\n131: \n132: * The new ``redirect_authenticated_user`` parameter for the\n133:   ``django.contrib.auth.views.login()`` view allows redirecting\n134:   authenticated users visiting the login page.\n135: \n136: * The new :class:`~django.contrib.auth.backends.AllowAllUsersModelBackend` and\n137:   :class:`~django.contrib.auth.backends.AllowAllUsersRemoteUserBackend` ignore\n138:   the value of ``User.is_active``, while\n139:   :class:`~django.contrib.auth.backends.ModelBackend` and\n140:   :class:`~django.contrib.auth.backends.RemoteUserBackend` now reject inactive\n141:   users.\n142: \n143: :mod:`django.contrib.gis`\n144: ~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~\n145: \n146: * :ref:`Distance lookups <distance-lookups>` now accept expressions as the\n147:   distance value parameter.\n148: \n149: * The new :attr:`GEOSGeometry.unary_union\n150:   <django.contrib.gis.geos.GEOSGeometry.unary_union>` property computes the\n151:   union of all the elements of this geometry.\n152: \n153: * Added the :meth:`GEOSGeometry.covers()\n154:   <django.contrib.gis.geos.GEOSGeometry.covers>` binary predicate.\n155: \n156: * Added the :meth:`GDALBand.statistics()\n157:   <django.contrib.gis.gdal.GDALBand.statistics>` method and\n158:   :attr:`~django.contrib.gis.gdal.GDALBand.mean`\n159:   and :attr:`~django.contrib.gis.gdal.GDALBand.std` attributes.\n160: \n161: * Added support for the :class:`~django.contrib.gis.db.models.MakeLine`\n162:   aggregate and :class:`~django.contrib.gis.db.models.functions.GeoHash`\n163:   function on SpatiaLite.\n164: \n165: * Added support for the\n166:   :class:`~django.contrib.gis.db.models.functions.Difference`,\n167:   :class:`~django.contrib.gis.db.models.functions.Intersection`, and\n168:   :class:`~django.contrib.gis.db.models.functions.SymDifference`\n169:   functions on MySQL.\n170: \n171: * Added support for instantiating empty GEOS geometries.\n172: \n173: * The new :attr:`~django.contrib.gis.geos.WKTWriter.trim` and\n174:   :attr:`~django.contrib.gis.geos.WKTWriter.precision` properties\n175:   of :class:`~django.contrib.gis.geos.WKTWriter` allow controlling\n176:   output of the fractional part of the coordinates in WKT.\n177: \n178: * Added the :attr:`LineString.closed\n179:   <django.contrib.gis.geos.LineString.closed>` and\n180:   :attr:`MultiLineString.closed\n181:   <django.contrib.gis.geos.MultiLineString.closed>` properties.\n182: \n183: * The :doc:`GeoJSON serializer </ref/contrib/gis/serializers>` now outputs the\n184:   primary key of objects in the ``properties`` dictionary if specific fields\n185:   aren't specified.\n186: \n187: * The ability to replicate input data on the :meth:`GDALBand.data()\n188:   <django.contrib.gis.gdal.GDALBand.data>` method was added. Band data can\n189:   now be updated with repeated values efficiently.\n190: \n191: * Added database functions\n192:   :class:`~django.contrib.gis.db.models.functions.IsValid` and\n193:   :class:`~django.contrib.gis.db.models.functions.MakeValid`, as well as the\n194:   :lookup:`isvalid` lookup, all for PostGIS. This allows filtering and\n195:   repairing invalid geometries on the database side.\n196: \n197: * Added raster support for all :doc:`spatial lookups\n198:   </ref/contrib/gis/geoquerysets>`.\n199: \n200: :mod:`django.contrib.postgres`\n201: ","url":"https://sourcegraph.sourcegraph.com/github.com/sg-evals/django--674eda1c@674eda1c03a3187905f48afee0f15226aa62fdf3/-/blob/docs/releases/1.10.txt%3FL1-200"}}}

Django lets you design URLs however you want, with no framework\\n7: limitations.\\n8: \\n9: See `Cool URIs don't change`_, by World Wide Web creator Tim Berners-Lee, for\\n10: excellent arguments on why URLs should be clean and usable.\\n11: \\n12: .. _Cool URIs don't change: https://www.w3.org/Provider/Style/URI\\n13: \\n14: Overview\\n15: ========\\n16: \\n17: To design URLs for an app, you create a Python module informally called a\\n18: **URLconf** (URL configuration). This module is pure Python code and is a\\n19: mapping between URL path expressions to Python functions (your views).\\n20: \\n21: This mapping can be as short or as long as needed. It can reference other\\n22: mappings. And, because it's pure Python code, it can be constructed\\n23: dynamically.\\n24: \\n25: Django also provides a way to translate URLs according to the active\\n26: language. See the :ref:`internationalization documentation\\n27: <url-internationalization>` for more information.\\n28: \\n29: .. _how-django-processes-a-request:\\n30: \\n31: How Django processes a request\\n32: ==============================\\n33: \\n34: When a user requests a page from your Django-powered site, this is the\\n35: algorithm the system follows to determine which Python code to execute:\\n36: \\n37: #. Django determines the root URLconf module to use. Ordinarily, this is the\\n38:    value of the :setting:`ROOT_URLCONF` setting, but if the incoming\\n39:    ``HttpRequest`` object has a :attr:`~django.http.HttpRequest.urlconf`\\n40:    attribute (set by middleware), its value will be used in place of the\\n41:    :setting:`ROOT_URLCONF` setting.\\n42: \\n43: #. Django loads that Python module and looks for the variable\\n44:    ``urlpatterns``. This should be a :term:`sequence` of\\n45:    :func:`django.urls.path` and/or :func:`django.urls.re_path` instances.\\n46: \\n47: #. Django runs through each URL pattern, in order, and stops at the first\\n48:    one that matches the requested URL, matching against\\n49:    :attr:`~django.http.HttpRequest.path_info`.\\n50: \\n51: #. Once one of the URL patterns matches, Django imports and calls the given\\n52:    view, which is a Python function (or a :doc:`class-based view\\n53:    </topics/class-based-views/index>`). The view gets passed the following\\n54:    arguments:\\n55: \\n56:    * An instance of :class:`~django.http.HttpRequest`.\\n57:    * If the matched URL pattern contained no named groups, then the\\n58:      matches from the regular expression are provided as positional arguments.\\n59:    * The keyword arguments are made up of any named parts matched by the\\n60:      path expression that are provided, overridden by any arguments specified\\n61:      in the optional ``kwargs`` argument to :func:`django.urls.path` or\\n62:      :func:`django.urls.re_path`.\\n63: \\n64: #. If no URL pattern matches, or if an exception is raised during any\\n65:    point in this process, Django invokes an appropriate\\n66:    error-handling view. See `Error handling`_ below.\\n67: \\n68: Example\\n69: =======\\n70: \\n71: Here's a sample URLconf::\\n72: \\n73:     from django.urls import path\\n74: \\n75:     from . import views\\n76: \\n77:     urlpatterns = [\\n78:         path(\\\"articles/2003/\\\", views.special_case_2003),\\n79:         path(\\\"articles/<int:year>/\\\", views.year_archive),\\n80:         path(\\\"articles/<int:year>/<int:month>/\\\", views.month_archive),\\n81:         path(\\\"articles/<int:year>/<int:month>/<slug:slug>/\\\", views.article_detail),\\n82:     ]\\n83: \\n84: Notes:\\n85: \\n86: * To capture a value from the URL, use angle brackets.\\n87: \\n88: * Captured values can optionally include a converter type. For example, use\\n89:   ``<int:name>`` to capture an integer parameter. If a converter isn't\\n90:   included, any string, excluding a ``/`` character, is matched.\\n91: \\n92: * There's no need to add a leading slash, because every URL has that. For\\n93:   example, it's ``articles``, not ``/articles``.\\n94: \\n95: Example requests:\\n96: \\n97: * A request to ``/articles/2005/03/`` would match the third entry in the\\n98:   list. Django would call the function\\n99:   ``views.month_archive(request, year=2005, month=3)``.\\n100: \\n101: * ``/articles/2003/`` would match the first pattern in the list, not the\\n102:   second one, because the patterns are tested in order, and the first one\\n103:   is the first test to pass. Feel free to exploit the ordering to insert\\n104:   special cases like this. Here, Django would call the function\\n105:   ``views.special_case_2003(request)``\\n106: \\n107: * ``/articles/2003`` would not match any of these patterns, because each\\n108:   pattern requires that the URL end with a slash.\\n109: \\n110: * ``/articles/2003/03/building-a-django-site/`` would match the final pattern.\\n111:   Django would call the function\\n112:   ``views.article_detail(request, year=2003, month=3, slug=\\\"building-a-django-site\\\")``.\\n113: \\n114: Path converters\\n115: ===============\\n116: \\n117: The following path converters are available by default:\\n118: \\n119: * ``str`` - Matches any non-empty string, excluding the path separator,\\n120:   ``'/'``. This is the default if a converter isn't included in the expression.\\n121: \\n122: * ``int`` - Matches zero or any positive integer. Returns an ``int``.\\n123: \\n124: * ``slug`` - Matches any slug string consisting of ASCII letters or numbers,\\n125:   plus the hyphen and underscore characters. For example,\\n126:   ``building-your-1st-django-site``.\\n127: \\n128: * ``uuid`` - Matches a formatted UUID. To prevent multiple URLs from mapping to\\n129:   the same page, dashes must be included and letters must be lowercase. For\\n130:   example, ``075194d3-6885-417e-a8a8-6c931e272f00``. Returns a\\n131:   :class:`~uuid.UUID` instance.\\n132: \\n133: * ``path`` - Matches any non-empty string, including the path separator,\\n134:   ``'/'``. This allows you to match against a complete URL path rather than\\n135:   a segment of a URL path as with ``str``.\\n136: \\n137: .. _registering-custom-path-converters:\\n138: \\n139: Registering custom path converters\\n140: ==================================\\n141: \\n142: For more complex matching requirements, you can define your own path\\n143: converters.\\n144: \\n145: A converter is a class that includes the following:\\n146: \\n147: * A ``regex`` class attribute, as a string.\\n148: \\n149: * A ``to_python(self, value)`` method, which handles converting the matched\\n150:   string into the type that should be passed to the view function. Django loads that Python module and looks for the variable\n44:    ``urlpatterns``. This should be a :term:`sequence` of\n45:    :func:`django.urls.path` and/or :func:`django.urls.re_path` instances.\n46: \n47: #. Django runs through each URL pattern, in order, and stops at the first\n48:    one that matches the requested URL, matching against\n49:    :attr:`~django.http.HttpRequest.path_info`.\n50: \n51: #. Once one of the URL patterns matches, Django imports and calls the given\n52:    view, which is a Python function (or a :doc:`class-based view\n53:    </topics/class-based-views/index>`). The view gets passed the following\n54:    arguments:\n55: \n56:    * An instance of :class:`~django.http.HttpRequest`.\n57:    * If the matched URL pattern contained no named groups, then the\n58:      matches from the regular expression are provided as positional arguments.\n59:    * The keyword arguments are made up of any named parts matched by the\n60:      path expression that are provided, overridden by any arguments specified\n61:      in the optional ``kwargs`` argument to :func:`django.urls.path` or\n62:      :func:`django.urls.re_path`.\n63: \n64: #. If no URL pattern matches, or if an exception is raised during any\n65:    point in this process, Django invokes an appropriate\n66:    error-handling view. See `Error handling`_ below.\n67: \n68: Example\n69: =======\n70: \n71: Here's a sample URLconf::\n72: \n73:     from django.urls import path\n74: \n75:     from . import views\n76: \n77:     urlpatterns = [\n78:         path(\"articles/2003/\", views.special_case_2003),\n79:         path(\"articles/<int:year>/\", views.year_archive),\n80:         path(\"articles/<int:year>/<int:month>/\", views.month_archive),\n81:         path(\"articles/<int:year>/<int:month>/<slug:slug>/\", views.article_detail),\n82:     ]\n83: \n84: Notes:\n85: \n86: * To capture a value from the URL, use angle brackets.\n87: \n88: * Captured values can optionally include a converter type. For example, use\n89:   ``<int:name>`` to capture an integer parameter. If a converter isn't\n90:   included, any string, excluding a ``/`` character, is matched.\n91: \n92: * There's no need to add a leading slash, because every URL has that. For\n93:   example, it's ``articles``, not ``/articles``.\n94: \n95: Example requests:\n96: \n97: * A request to ``/articles/2005/03/`` would match the third entry in the\n98:   list. Django would call the function\n99:   ``views.month_archive(request, year=2005, month=3)``.\n100: \n101: * ``/articles/2003/`` would match the first pattern in the list, not the\n102:   second one, because the patterns are tested in order, and the first one\n103:   is the first test to pass. Feel free to exploit the ordering to insert\n104:   special cases like this. Here, Django would call the function\n105:   ``views.special_case_2003(request)``\n106: \n107: * ``/articles/2003`` would not match any of these patterns, because each\n108:   pattern requires that the URL end with a slash.\n109: \n110: * ``/articles/2003/03/building-a-django-site/`` would match the final pattern.\n111:   Django would call the function\n112:   ``views.article_detail(request, year=2003, month=3, slug=\"building-a-django-site\")``.\n113: \n114: Path converters\n115: ===============\n116: \n117: The following path converters are available by default:\n118: \n119: * ``str`` - Matches any non-empty string, excluding the path separator,\n120:   ``'/'``. This is the default if a converter isn't included in the expression.\n121: \n122: * ``int`` - Matches zero or any positive integer. Returns an ``int``.\n123: \n124: * ``slug`` - Matches any slug string consisting of ASCII letters or numbers,\n125:   plus the hyphen and underscore characters. For example,\n126:   ``building-your-1st-django-site``.\n127: \n128: * ``uuid`` - Matches a formatted UUID. To prevent multiple URLs from mapping to\n129:   the same page, dashes must be included and letters must be lowercase. For\n130:   example, ``075194d3-6885-417e-a8a8-6c931e272f00``. Returns a\n131:   :class:`~uuid.UUID` instance.\n132: \n133: * ``path`` - Matches any non-empty string, including the path separator,\n134:   ``'/'``. This allows you to match against a complete URL path rather than\n135:   a segment of a URL path as with ``str``.\n136: \n137: .. _registering-custom-path-converters:\n138: \n139: Registering custom path converters\n140: ==================================\n141: \n142: For more complex matching requirements, you can define your own path\n143: converters.\n144: \n145: A converter is a class that includes the following:\n146: \n147: * A ``regex`` class attribute, as a string.\n148: \n149: * A ``to_python(self, value)`` method, which handles converting the matched\n150:   string into the type that should be passed to the view function. It should\n151: ","url":"https://sourcegraph.sourcegraph.com/github.com/sg-evals/django--674eda1c@674eda1c03a3187905f48afee0f15226aa62fdf3/-/blob/docs/topics/http/urls.txt%3FL1-150"}}}

\"django/urls/base.py\", \"symbol\": \"reverse\"}\n  ],\n  \"text\": \"## Django URL Routing Implementation\\n\\nThe Django URL routing system has evolved from the legacy `patterns()` function (removed in Django 1.10) to the modern `path()` and `re_path()` based approach. Here are the key components:\\n\\n### Core URL Configuration (django/urls/conf.py)\\nThe `include()` function (line 17-59) processes URL module references by extracting the `urlpatterns` attribute from imported modules and handling app_name and namespace configurations. It supports both string module paths and direct module/list references. The `_path()` function (line 62-92) is the foundation for both `path` and `re_path`, creating either URLResolver objects (for include() results, which are lists/tuples) or URLPattern objects (for view callables).\\n\\n### URL Pattern Objects (django/urls/resolvers.py)\\n**URLPattern** (line 422-501): Represents a single URL pattern with a pattern (regex or route), callback view, default arguments, and name. It includes a `resolve()` method that matches incoming paths against the pattern and returns a ResolverMatch.\\n\\n**URLResolver** (line 503-850+): The main dispatcher that recursively processes URL hierarchies. It manages url_patterns (both URLPattern and nested URLResolver instances), handles namespace resolution, and implements the core URL matching algorithm via its `resolve()` method. The `_populate()` method (line 545-627) builds lookup dictionaries for reverse URL resolution.\\n\\n**Pattern Classes**:\\n- **RegexPattern** (line 192-240): Matches URLs using Python regex with support for named and unnamed groups\\n- **RoutePattern** (line 314-386): Modern path syntax using angle-bracket converters like `<int:id>`\\n- **LocalePrefixPattern** (line 388-420): Used by i18n_patterns() for language prefix handling\\n\\n### Path Converters (django/urls/converters.py)\\nProvides IntConverter, StringConverter, SlugConverter, UUIDConverter, and PathConverter with `to_python()` and `to_url()` methods for parameter conversion. Custom converters can be registered via `register_converter()`.\\n\\n### URL Resolution Process (django/urls/base.py)\\nThe `resolve()` function (line 22-25) delegates to URLResolver.resolve() which:\\n1. Matches the request path against patterns in order\\n2. Returns a ResolverMatch with the view function and captured parameters\\n3. It supports both string module paths and direct module/list references.
